uri='https://www.blogger.com'>Blogger</generator><openSearch:totalResults>2852</openSearch:totalResults><openSearch:startIndex>26</openSearch:startIndex><openSearch:itemsPerPage>25</openSearch:itemsPerPage><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-4457992550572389543</id><published>2016-01-26T09:07:00.001-08:00</published><updated>2016-01-26T09:14:20.685-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='paul watson'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='whale wars'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='sea shepherd media garbage'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='conservation fraud'/><title type='text'>Paul Watson and the sinking of the "Ady Gil"</title><content type='html'>There are a lot of conservation organizations out there, all looking to raise money for their causes. It's rare that you see a call to sign a petition etc. that is not automatically asking you for money, after you signed it. There is nothing inherently wrong with asking for money, because there are cost involved with saving the oceans. With some groups however, making money seems to be the main purpose, regardless of who, or what they hurt in the process. Take the following example.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In 2010 the "&lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MY_Ady_Gil"&gt;Ady Gil&lt;/a&gt;", a small vessel operated by the &lt;a href="http://www.seashepherd.org/"&gt;Sea Shepherd Conservation Society&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp; collided with the Japanese whaling ship "&lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MV_Sh%C5%8Dnan_Maru_2"&gt;Shonan Maru 2&lt;/a&gt;" and sank some time later. "SSCS" has always claimed that the collision damage inflicted on the "Ady Gil" is what caused her to sink and maintained that the Japanese intentionally rammed their vessel.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There is video evidence that the collision itself was actually caused by the captain of the "Ady Gil", by accelerating into the path of the "Shonan Maru 2" at the last moment. In this video, you can see that the "Ady Gil" is stopped in the water and a little before the collision there is whitewater behind the vessel, a sign that it engaged the props and accelerated forward, right into the path of the Japanese ship.&amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="300" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/MbGDNkjFUGo" width="530"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt; This video has led some people to accuse SCCS of intentionally causing this accident to create publicity for their "Whale Wars" TV show and to raise money from their supporters. I'm not accusing the captain of the "Ady Gil" of trying to intentionally ram the Japanese ship. While I think it's more likely that he wanted to cut right in front of it to get some dramatic TV footage and simply miscalculated, the claim that SSCS created this whole event gained some credibility, when in the aftermath of the sinking, &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Bethune"&gt;Pete Bethune&lt;/a&gt;, the captain of the "Ady Gil" came out and stated that he deliberately sank the vessel on the orders of &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Watson"&gt;Paul Watson&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Sea Shepherd maintained that the "Ady Gil" sank because of the damage it sustained during the collision and that they made every effort to save it.&amp;nbsp; In reply to Bethune's admission, the SSCS released this &lt;a href="http://www.seashepherd.org/commentary-and-editorials/2010/10/08/the-biggest-sea-shepherd-non-story-of-the-year-57"&gt;statement&lt;/a&gt; by Watson. In part it read: &lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;"So why has Bethune decided to make such an accusation to the media and the public that I ordered him to sink the Ady Gil?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;The answer is obvious. I fired him the day before for providing false  statements to the Japanese police. He then threatened to make this  allegation against me if I did not reinstate him. I refused. In fact, I  sent Bethune’s threats to the media before he released them."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;After hearing Bethune's confession,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/ady.gil?fref=ts"&gt;Ady Gil&lt;/a&gt;, a person who donated 1 Million $ to the SSCS and who the boat was named after, ended up &lt;a href="http://www.3news.co.nz/world/ady-gil-sues-sea-shepherd-over-antarctic-sinking-2013011013#axzz3xuJMY9Ot"&gt;suing&lt;/a&gt; them for the loss of the vessel. After years of back and forth, last September, the arbitrator in this case issued finally issued a &lt;a href="http://www.ady.com/Award-Final_Award-Kalicki.pdf"&gt;ruling&lt;/a&gt; that now became public.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 19"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;The ruling includes a scathing assessment of Paul Watson: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"The Arbitrator found Mr. Watson’s testimony regarding certain events to be highly evasive, internally contradictory, or at odds with his own prior written statements, and in certain areas simply lacking the basic indicia of genuineness that instinctively inspires confidence and trust" &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;           &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So now we know that &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Watson"&gt;Paul Watson&lt;/a&gt; ordered the deliberate sinking of the "Ady Gil"&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A couple of days ago, &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/Chuck-Swift-181726158584822/?fref=nf"&gt;Chuck Swift&lt;/a&gt;, former captain of the Sea Shepherd vessel "Bob Barker" also came out and admitted publicly that the "Ady Gil" was intentionally sunk and issued a public apology on Facebook, for his role in it.&amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;YES. I, along with Pete Bethune and Luke VanHorn, did board the vessel  Ady Gil and intentionally scuttled it. We sank the vessel Ady Gil and  lied to everyone inside and outside of SSCS to cover that truth.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;You can read his entire statement &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/permalink.php?story_fbid=935202239903873&amp;amp;id=181726158584822"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Why was it so important to Paul Watson to sink the "Ady Gil"? &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;Before acceding to Mr. Watson’s demands, &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;(to deliberately scuttle the vessel)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt; Mr. Swift recalls that he asked Mr. Watson, “Why is this so important to you?”, and Mr. Watson responded, “Our audience needs closure.”&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 8.000000pt; vertical-align: 6.000000pt;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt; I guess this illustrates&amp;nbsp; where Paul Watson's priorities are.  Entertaining his audience is more important than what he claims to care  about. Of course Watson had no qualms about the fact that the "closure"  he provided to his TV audience was a blatant lie and he didn't hesitate  to use that lie to raise money.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;From the ruling: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Of course, whatever the rationale for deceiving the viewing public  (which might be presumed to understand that “reality shows” do not  actually reflect reality) &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here are some excerpts from the arbitrators ruling, that offer insight into the reasons the SSCS wanted to scuttle the "Ady Gil" and how "real" "whale wars" really is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;the evidence suggests that the Ady Gil was unlikely to sink for any appreciable period of time, notwithstanding the damage she incurred from the collision with the Japanese fleet&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;the crew’s thinking &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;(to scuttle to Ady Gil)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt; seems to have been directly influenced by the presence of the Animal Planet film crew, which gave SSCS unparalleled public exposure and greatly expanded its fundraising possibilities. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;nbsp;   &lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;Certainly, a plodding tow operation to deliver a damaged vessel to shore would not have made for interesting television viewing&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;               &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;By contrast, the collision of the Shonan Maru #2 with the Ady Gil already had captured unparalleled media attention, with Mr. Watson giving interviews from the Steve Irwin and Pete Bethune taking non-stop media calls on board the Bob Barker. The crew was&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt; acutely aware that the sinking of the Ady Gil would create the occasion for more dramatic reality television &lt;/span&gt;           &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 47"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;   &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;    &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;     &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;Indeed, Mr. Swift testifies that “during our discussions/arguments leading up to my capitulation to Paul’s order to sink the Ady Gil, he was telling me ... ‘Oh, the media on this would be great.’”&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;               &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 47"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;   &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;    &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;     &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;Paul’s a genius, and he’s a media genius especially. And sometimes he’s open-minded, and sometimes, he’s not. And, when he sets his mind on something he’s like a pit bull getting lock jaw, and I was unable to change his mind, which is why I eventually executed his orders&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;               &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 49"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;As for the scene in "Whale Wars", where Bethune and Swift discussed abandoning the ship: &lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;The decision to stage this scene for the cameras was the result of discussions between Mr. Bethune and Mr. Swift, in the presence of the Animal Planet crew:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt; they said we need to just create the scene that makes it look like you were making the decision to abandon the boat. And I knew from Whale War’s perspective, ... the decision to abandon a boat by the captain is a pretty powerful scene. I went along with it &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;    &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;               &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;The arbitrator offered this thought. &lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;Of course, whatever the rationale for deceiving the viewing public (which might be presumed to understand that “reality shows” do not actually reflect reality), there was no legal or moral justification for deceiving Claimants, the owners of the Ady Gil.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;So we know that SSCS and Paul Watson have no problem deceiving their supporters and the viewers of "Whale Wars" who think that the series is an actual documentary. What is interesting to find out is that they equally have no problem with throwing their own employees, donors and volunteers under the bus, blaming them for their own actions.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;There are many great organizations working to save the oceans and it's inhabitant and I encourage to support them. Just check them out carefully before you choose which one you want to support.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 32"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;timesnewroman&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/4457992550572389543/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=4457992550572389543' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/4457992550572389543'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/4457992550572389543'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2016/01/paul-watson-and-sinking-of-ady-gil.html' title='Paul Watson and the sinking of the &quot;Ady Gil&quot;'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='https://img.youtube.com/vi/MbGDNkjFUGo/default.jpg' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-3662425255889252711</id><published>2016-01-18T12:03:00.001-08:00</published><updated>2016-01-18T12:03:56.696-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark in a pool'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='animal cruelty'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='saving sharks'/><title type='text'>Sharks in a pool?</title><content type='html'>After the movie "Jaws" came out in 1975, a lot of people were afraid to even enter a pool or a bathtub. Who knew that one could actually find a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; in a pool?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Check out this story. &lt;a href="http://www.sun-sentinel.com/local/palm-beach/fl-pool-shark-update-20160117-story.html"&gt;A shark found in a swimming pool!&lt;/a&gt; According to an article in Florida's "&lt;a href="http://www.sun-sentinel.com/"&gt;Sun Sentinel&lt;/a&gt;" Nicole Bonk found a 5 foot blacktip shark in a pool. &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-i9uU3qk75dA/Vp1ClZGWKWI/AAAAAAAACKQ/3qpIACfm4dc/s1600/IMG_9492.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-i9uU3qk75dA/Vp1ClZGWKWI/AAAAAAAACKQ/3qpIACfm4dc/s400/IMG_9492.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Blacktip shark ©Martin Graf&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;"Nicole Bonk was visiting friends at the Mariner's Cay condo the week  before last when she saw two boys carrying the five-foot blacktip shark,  with hooks in its mouth, and dump it into the pool at around 11 p.m."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;She and her husband pulled the shark out and carried it to the  Intracoastal Waterway, where her husband held the shark by the tail in  the water so it could try to flush out the chlorinated pool water. Then  they released it.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"We tried to revive him but he mostly likely did  not live," she said. "He was barely moving after the trauma. We did our  best to try to save this creature."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;It's really disturbing that these kids had so little regard for a living creature. I'm glad that Nicole Bonk and her husband tried to save the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; and hope that it survived.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;This story shows that human beings are both capable of cruelty and compassion. I'm glad that the "Sun Sentinel" focused it's article on those issues and not on trying to scare people into thinking they have to be afraid to enter a pool.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I hope that they find the kids who did this and teach them that this is not acceptable behavior.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;She reported the incident to the Florida Fish and Wildlife  Conservation Commission, but no officers arrived until the following  morning.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"These two kids, they came back from fishing and threw  this half-dead creature into the pool as a prank," she said. "They left  the shark in the pool to die. I think they're terrible children because  it's animal cruelty."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;The wildlife commission is investigating the  incident and attempting to find evidence from video security cameras  around the pool.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='bull shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Beqa Lagoon'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Beqa Adventure Divers'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='fiji'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark reef marine reserve'/><title type='text'>Conservation shark diving in Fiji</title><content type='html'>This is the 4th year &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; is going to Fiji to dive with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;Bull Sharks&lt;/a&gt; at Beqa &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdive.com/conservation/shark-reef-marine-reserve/"&gt;Shark Reef Marine Reserve&lt;/a&gt;. In the last 3 years, we have been diving with more than 70 Bull Sharks at a time, with Black Tip-, White Tip-, Grey Reef-, Nurse- and Lemon-Sharks also being seen on almost every dive. Occasionally we even got a visit from a Tiger Shark.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jlG8YSanWKE/U35NLo1fPsI/AAAAAAAAA5M/GK_PtPMYMk0/s1600/XD5V1869-293.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jlG8YSanWKE/U35NLo1fPsI/AAAAAAAAA5M/GK_PtPMYMk0/s400/XD5V1869-293.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While I love "my" Great White Sharks, I have to say that it is hard to beat the excitement of what Ron and Valery Taylor called "The best shark dive in the world".&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-QEiXAP98Ic0/U35OP3ga7TI/AAAAAAAAA48/-CpUN98Y2-s/s1600/XD5V0095.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="242" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-QEiXAP98Ic0/U35OP3ga7TI/AAAAAAAAA48/-CpUN98Y2-s/s400/XD5V0095.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Our partner in Fiji is Beqa Adventure Divers "&lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;BAD&lt;/a&gt;". BAD is truly an exceptionally GOOD dive operation who was instrumental in creating the &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdive.com/conservation/shark-reef-marine-reserve/"&gt;Shark Reef Marine Reserve&lt;/a&gt;, which is now officially a &lt;a href="http://wwf.panda.org/?232510/Fiji-spearheading-global-shark-conservation"&gt;national marine&lt;/a&gt; park and fully protected.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="281" mozallowfullscreen="" src="https://player.vimeo.com/video/110873549" webkitallowfullscreen="" width="500"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;a href="https://vimeo.com/110873549"&gt;Celebration - BAD Cut&lt;/a&gt; from &lt;a href="https://vimeo.com/user2528821"&gt;Beqa Adventure Divers&lt;/a&gt; on &lt;a href="https://vimeo.com/"&gt;Vimeo&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;BAD&lt;/a&gt; is so good that the government of Fiji has designated them to be the official caretakers of the park, with their staff being the designated &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2009/03/back-to-school.html"&gt;fish wardens&lt;/a&gt;, empowered to enforce the rules of the park.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Jmxy6uYpagM/U35NjAqIt6I/AAAAAAAAA5I/hdhyxjrYgIQ/s1600/XD5V3443-181.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Jmxy6uYpagM/U35NjAqIt6I/AAAAAAAAA5I/hdhyxjrYgIQ/s400/XD5V3443-181.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;BAD&lt;/a&gt; is also a carbon neutral operation that supports the &lt;a href="http://mangrovesforfiji.com/about-us/"&gt;Mangroves for Fiji&lt;/a&gt;, a vital project that not only helps to offset carbon emissions, but also provides a crucial habitat for many marine creatures, including sharks.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-jCm23NlS9_I/VW5K6fsZo9I/AAAAAAAABb0/OdEYGTLQChw/s1600/_26A6811.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-jCm23NlS9_I/VW5K6fsZo9I/AAAAAAAABb0/OdEYGTLQChw/s400/_26A6811.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;BAD describes itself as "a conservation project masquerading as a dive shop" and they really mean it. They are a prime example for how conservation and business can not only coexist, but actually be mutually beneficial. One of the ways they make sure that the project works is by not only paying a levy to the fishing villages in exchange for them to not fish at the reef, but also by hiring their staff from those villages to provide an alternative income to the villagers. All the dive staff at &lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;BAD&lt;/a&gt; is from those local fishing villages. To see how the project works, &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdive.com/conservation/fiji-shark-project/"&gt;click here.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-exkHZaLwHHo/VW5JDK8zaII/AAAAAAAABbo/Q8YIziy6Qt0/s1600/_26A6192.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-exkHZaLwHHo/VW5JDK8zaII/AAAAAAAABbo/Q8YIziy6Qt0/s400/_26A6192.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; is diving in Fiji from May 8 - 29. A 7 day stay (5 days of shark diving), is starting at $1800 p/p double occupancy. The price includes 7 nights accommodation in a 4 star hotel, with a breakfast buffet edaily, 5 days of 2 tank shark diving and rt. airport transportation from Nadi airport.  We can customize your dates and length of stay and also add some dives in the soft coral capital of the world. Cost of airfare from LA to Fiji varies from $1000 to about $1300, depending on day of departure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We can also book your shark dive with "BAD" anytime of the year, with or without a hotel. Call us at 619.887.4275 or email staff@sharkdiver.com for more info, or to book.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FBzTfEbvh94/VYcxZSrnN-I/AAAAAAAABgI/culXBsfcwM8/s1600/_26A3001.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FBzTfEbvh94/VYcxZSrnN-I/AAAAAAAABgI/culXBsfcwM8/s400/_26A3001.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver &lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. term='Marine conservation science institute'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Support shark conservation at Guadalupe Island</title><content type='html'>With the holidays fast approaching, what are you going to give the person who has everything? Here is an idea. Sponsor, or name a shark at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; and support the research and conservation efforts there.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/"&gt;Marine Conservation Science Institute&lt;/a&gt; is not only maintaining a &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/white-shark/"&gt;photo ID database&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;, but also does extensive research into the migration behavior of "our" &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt;. By naming, or sponsoring a shark, you are helping to keep the research going.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let me introduce #153 from our database. He's an awesome shark and I hope that you agree that #153 is not a good name for this guy. I'm sure you can come up with something better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-SG9sTPI6rRA/Vmd3K5V4RDI/AAAAAAAACH4/EIqU89PP31Y/s1600/_26A5839%2BShark%2B%2523153-2.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="261" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-SG9sTPI6rRA/Vmd3K5V4RDI/AAAAAAAACH4/EIqU89PP31Y/s400/_26A5839%2BShark%2B%2523153-2.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To name or sponsor this awesome individual, visit &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/donations/"&gt;http://www.marinecsi.org/donations/&lt;/a&gt;. All the proceeds go to the research and your donation is fully tax deductible.&lt;br /&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-WDQTtGr8298/Vg0GrO5i6CI/AAAAAAAAB28/yplyLWfopjc/s1600/_26A5834%2BShark%2B%2523153%2Bcopy.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-WDQTtGr8298/Vg0GrO5i6CI/AAAAAAAAB28/yplyLWfopjc/s400/_26A5834%2BShark%2B%2523153%2Bcopy.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are the one that ends up naming this shark,&amp;nbsp; &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; will give you a print of either one of these pictures, so you can show your friends the shark you named.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/6775722215072922630/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=6775722215072922630' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-SG9sTPI6rRA/Vmd3K5V4RDI/AAAAAAAACH4/EIqU89PP31Y/s72-c/_26A5839%2BShark%2B%2523153-2.JPG' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-4609284424601689915</id><published>2015-12-03T10:47:00.000-08:00</published><updated>2015-12-03T10:47:15.747-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Nicole Lucas-Nasby'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark science'/><title type='text'>Science Expedition to Guadalupe Island</title><content type='html'>I booked the trip to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; (Guadalupe Island) with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; of San Diego to fulfill a long held desire – since reading  Jacques-Yves Cousteau’s “The &lt;span class="text_exposed_show"&gt;Shark” and  meeting his son in San Diego when I was a boy. And, in every way  possible, this trip exceeded my expectations owing to the efforts of an  outstanding Shark Diver team (particularly Martin Graf and Cindy  Michaels), the Guest Marine Researcher Nicole Nasby Lucas, a fantastic  Horizon crew, and great group of fellow &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark divers&lt;/a&gt;. This is a must do  in my opinion for anyone with a passion, interest or bucket list item relating to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt; – it’s fun, safe and amazing. Many details follow.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="text_exposed_show"&gt; The Main Event:&lt;br /&gt;  I don’t want to bury the lead, so I’ll get right to our guests of  honor. The &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt; are impressive, majestic, and beautiful.  They move by the twin cages, quite closely, at a stately pace, and look  at the folks in the cage with large deep blue eyes; and, they appear  utterly calm and in command. They make passes at the two bait carcasses  off the stern, sometimes lazily and on occasion quite quickly. We were  fortunate enough to witness a breach on one occasion – a male, who had  previously made half-hearted passes at the bait, disappeared, the  emerged from deep below the boat, under the cages, at speed, and hit the  bait vertically from below, taking himself halfway out of the water –  to the astonishment, screams and overwhelming joy of everyone aboard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-wgy8y6Gbdh8/VXHx5UIUIfI/AAAAAAAABdk/cSiWuhSdeCE/s1600/1-8%2B6.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-wgy8y6Gbdh8/VXHx5UIUIfI/AAAAAAAABdk/cSiWuhSdeCE/s400/1-8%2B6.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The visibility, typically, is very good at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;, so the sun  penetrates deep into the water and the boat casts a long shadow into the  depths. Often our first sightings each time into the cage(s) were of  the dark silhouette emerging from the shadow cast by the boat, coming up  slowly from below and then circling the cages, bait and boat for some  time before silently disappearing into the shadows again. Though each of  us kept eyes peeled in all directions, it was amazing how frequently we  were taken by surprise by a shark suddenly appearing. On deck, between  dives, the crew is very experienced and keen eyed; and, they will call  out “&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;White Shark&lt;/a&gt;” as they approach, usually well before any guests see  them. From above or below it is mesmerizing, and difficult to turn away.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bh62bMu5JnU/VlNb-5-btII/AAAAAAAACFA/QorEVQtwi8s/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.32.49%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="261" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bh62bMu5JnU/VlNb-5-btII/AAAAAAAACFA/QorEVQtwi8s/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.32.49%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;br /&gt;  There are a few places worldwide to see &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt; with  predictability. Both South Africa and the Farallon Islands offer this  opportunity; but, both have limited underwater visibility and  challenging water temperatures. &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; has better water clarity,  100 foot visibility, and weather, and very few (we saw only three  other) boats, some distance away. Unlike other locations, &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; will not force you to deal with cold and murky water, crowded boats and  cages, quick “in and out” quick thrill experiences, etc. You will have  days on the dive site, in relatively warm and very clear water, and good  weather.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-WDQTtGr8298/Vg0GrO5i6CI/AAAAAAAAB28/yplyLWfopjc/s1600/_26A5834%2BShark%2B%2523153%2Bcopy.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-WDQTtGr8298/Vg0GrO5i6CI/AAAAAAAAB28/yplyLWfopjc/s400/_26A5834%2BShark%2B%2523153%2Bcopy.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;#153 he needs a name! You can name him by clicking &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/sponsor-a-shark/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; is a designated &lt;a href="http://www2.cec.org/nampan/mpa/isla-guadalupe-biosphere-reserve"&gt;Bio Sphere&lt;/a&gt;, a marine  sanctuary. It sits about 200 miles southwest of San Diego. It is made up  of volcanic remnants and has a stark beauty, with tall, steep cliffs  diving hundreds of feet down to sea. There are large populations of, and  rookeries for, elephant seals, sea lions – all of which you are very  likely to see, with approaches to boat on occasion.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Timing:&lt;br /&gt;  Typically, though as Martin notes there are no hard and fast rules with  &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;White Sharks&lt;/a&gt;, they tell us the males will show up in earlier months –  e.g., July, August, and September – and in greater numbers. And the  typically October and November are when they have female sightings – the  females being fewer but much larger than the males. Also, typically,  the wetter weather comes later in the year, with the Pacific hurricane /  wet season; but, this too is not always the case.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; The Drive Out:&lt;br /&gt;  It is a long trip out to, and back from &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; from / to San  Diego. It was some eight hours from San Diego to Ensenada Mexico, where  we docked to have passports checked, and then a long 18 +/- hours to  &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;. Note that the return trip is the same itinerary, in  reverse, with a stop in Ensenada before entering U.S. waters. Along the  way out to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;, a large pod of dolphins escorted us. The sea can  often be a bit rough to quite rough, with good swells causing a fair bit  of roll onboard. Owing to timing, much of the initial leg is spent  hanging out in main cabin getting to know fellow divers, with folks  eventually heading to their beds – sleep and good anti motion sickness  remedies work well. Most folks used some combination of ear patch and  oral medication. It’s a long drive, so be smart and just bring your  meds.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-JTtrcdzExuk/VmCDwTccJ1I/AAAAAAAACGg/r0s4f-tUYBs/s1600/IMG_1780.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-JTtrcdzExuk/VmCDwTccJ1I/AAAAAAAACGg/r0s4f-tUYBs/s400/IMG_1780.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Boat:&lt;br /&gt; You won’t “Need bigger boat”&amp;nbsp;  The MV Horizon the Horizon is roughly 80 feet long with 8 state rooms  and several bunks. There are two restrooms and showers that are shared  by all. The accommodations (two persons to a room with curtain for  privacy and in bunks) are not lux, but they are nice, and you won’t care  anyway&amp;nbsp;  The Horizon is used only as diving vessel; and that's all season long.  They determine who bunks together once everyone arrives in San Diego,  based on number of couples, individual travelers, etc. The sleeping  quarters are below,, and the main cabin contains the galley and a series  of booths along each side used for dining and spending time together  with travelers in route or between dives. Net / net, this is a large and  comfortable boat.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ijetjC52kx8/Vdup1AQ3-XI/AAAAAAAABtQ/tB4GvMH2oH8/s1600/G0023723%2Barial%2Bwith%2Bshark.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="220" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ijetjC52kx8/Vdup1AQ3-XI/AAAAAAAABtQ/tB4GvMH2oH8/s400/G0023723%2Barial%2Bwith%2Bshark.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Cages:&lt;br /&gt; There are two, kept on deck  astern for the trip and each night when diving is completed. For each  day's diving, each is suspended off, but affixed to, the stern at the  surface (that is, they do not sink below) – so you simply climb down a  ladder and into the cage (easy); and each easily holds four divers. One  cage is aft port, one aft starboard. You will alternate each dive, so  that everyone has plenty of time in each cage.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-y2ahLW21sZg/Vdup0ZcjuAI/AAAAAAAABtM/psVCdGyxGYQ/s1600/GOPR0003-2.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="220" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-y2ahLW21sZg/Vdup0ZcjuAI/AAAAAAAABtM/psVCdGyxGYQ/s400/GOPR0003-2.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;nbsp;The Dives:&lt;br /&gt;  The divers are assigned to two teams. Each team dives for an hour, and  then rests and re-hydrates for an hour while the alternate team dives.  Each team has four people in each cage, and the team alternates cages  each time, so everyone gets to try both cages and gets plenty of dive  time and rest. There were a couple days of early open diving as well –  starting just after sunrise – during which anyone who preferred could  climb into either cage.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2fiJcxR5ZXk/VXHxlYKTPxI/AAAAAAAABdM/twayFcWbvwo/s1600/1-37.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2fiJcxR5ZXk/VXHxlYKTPxI/AAAAAAAABdM/twayFcWbvwo/s400/1-37.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The crew will size you for suits,  equipment, weights, and Martin himself oriented each of us to breathing  via air hose and made sure we comfortable before we stepped fully down  into the cage.&lt;br /&gt; Safety is primary and at no point was anything but  utterly assured all was well and well in control. No divers are ever  permitted out of the cages – for the sake of the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, the marine  preserve, as well as the divers. You are completely safe at all times.  There were folks of all ages, bith genders, and widely varying  experience levels. Past trips have included folks in their 60’s and  70’s, and quite young divers as well. The always amazing Cindy at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; can advise on particulars.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Breathing with the hookah system  is easy – no metal tanks to strap on, simply a long hose that goes from  on deck tank system to each diver’s regulator (mouthpiece through which  you breathe). So, if you’ve ever snorkeled and used a mask, you’ll be  just fine. The cages are beyond sturdy, offer complete visibility  around, above and below, and are plenty large enough for each set of  divers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aFlxEWsMIEc/VPX4Y4UviYI/AAAAAAAABS8/4Ti79gjTLoc/s1600/brianarnonesharkdiver.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="300" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aFlxEWsMIEc/VPX4Y4UviYI/AAAAAAAABS8/4Ti79gjTLoc/s400/brianarnonesharkdiver.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Purpose:&lt;br /&gt; In addition to the opportunity  provided to guests to see these amazing creatures, each shark observed  is photographed (Martin, Nicole and the divers get to participate in  this) and compared to a database of previously observed sharks. New  sharks are named and tracked in the database each successive year. This  is a joint effort between the &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/sponsor-a-shark/"&gt;Marine Conservation Science Institute &lt;/a&gt;(MCSI) and &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-zuxfTwtP3pY/VmCEwWxgxkI/AAAAAAAACGs/ibkABUaxBgY/s1600/%2523172%2BFreya%2B1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-zuxfTwtP3pY/VmCEwWxgxkI/AAAAAAAACGs/ibkABUaxBgY/s400/%2523172%2BFreya%2B1.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;#172 Freya a shark that was newly named this season.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Newly identified sharks on a particular  dive are named by the people on the dive in a bidding process (proceeds  of which go to the &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/sponsor-a-shark/"&gt;MCSI&lt;/a&gt; and shark research effort). On a side note, I  was fortunate enough from a 2014 dive with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; to name one –  Hooper (after the Richard Dreyfuss oceanographer character in Jaws) –  great fun and a great way to support the cause.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-b-4_CnmdILo/VmCG3BKVtWI/AAAAAAAACHA/aQIcG2YHNG4/s1600/_26A2733%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-b-4_CnmdILo/VmCG3BKVtWI/AAAAAAAACHA/aQIcG2YHNG4/s400/_26A2733%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;# 159 Hooper&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; is  home to a marine preserve and a research station manned by a researcher  named Mauricio – who will visit the Horizon and give an excellent  presentation with Martin on Great White Sharks and the Isla Guadalupe  Bio Sphere.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; The &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; Team:&lt;br /&gt; Martin Graf, the CEO and  dive leader, teacher, host is a deeply experienced and great guy. He is  hands on, overseeing everything on the dives. He also gives talks and a  presentation to the divers on &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt;, and  many experiences with both. If Nicole Nasby Lucas (again, researcher  from &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/sponsor-a-shark/"&gt;MCSI&lt;/a&gt;) is leading Science Expedition, she, too, will give a fine  presentation, talk. Both Martin and Nicole worked each evening on  identified sharks seen from photographs taken during the day. All the  reservations, logistics, arrangements, and care taking of the divers  before and after is led by the excellent and omnipresent Cindy Michaels,  their Director of Communications – Cindy was a rock star and took care  of every question and need leading up to the trip.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; The Horizon Crew:&lt;br /&gt;  In a word, excellent. Experienced captain, crew – professional, easy  going, genuinely friendly, and they take care of anything you might  need. I cannot say enough good things about the crew of the Horizon.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; The Food:&lt;br /&gt;  As noted elsewhere, the food is outstanding. The quality and quantity  of the meals is positively surprising and uniformly excellent. There is  also beer and wine aboard. There are large and delicious breakfasts  every morning cooked to order, excellent lunches (including Sashimi),  and absolutely fantastic dinners, including prime rib near end of stay.  The galley will account for you preferences and restrictions with no  problem.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;Thank you David Moore! We appreciate you taking the time to share your experience with us and our future divers. We are glad you enjoyed your expedition and hope to see you again on another shark trip.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver &lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-8235897978920576358</id><published>2015-11-24T09:42:00.001-08:00</published><updated>2015-11-24T09:42:17.373-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark cartilage'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark don&apos;t get cancer'/><title type='text'>Do sharks get cancer?</title><content type='html'>One of the reasons millions of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; get killed each year is the popular belief&amp;nbsp; that &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; don't get tumors, or cancer. That, along with the demand for &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; fins, are the major reasons sharks get slaughtered. The belief that &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; don't get cancer has led to a big demand for their cartilage, which is supposed to prevent, or cure cancer. Now I'm not a scientist, but it seems to me, that even if sharks were immune to cancer, eating their cartilage would not make me immune to it as well, just like eating a fish doesn't give me the ability to breathe underwater.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But are sharks really immune to tumors or cancer? Well, since I'm not a scientist, I'm not sure about the cancer part, but I can definitively say that sharks do get tumors. Take "Meli" for example. He's a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white shark&lt;/a&gt; who regularly visits &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. Last year we first spotted him with a big growth on his left side and it is still there a year later. These pictures were taken just a couple of weeks ago and show his big tumor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1IMvKt8e1hU/Vg0GgfYnSVI/AAAAAAAAB2E/AqkrhKHNflw/s1600/P9170039.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="225" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1IMvKt8e1hU/Vg0GgfYnSVI/AAAAAAAAB2E/AqkrhKHNflw/s400/P9170039.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-cLYDJzPMRac/Vg0GhFLv5GI/AAAAAAAAB2A/SGhMHeHIycI/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-09-17%2Bat%2B12.08.17%2BPM.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="245" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-cLYDJzPMRac/Vg0GhFLv5GI/AAAAAAAAB2A/SGhMHeHIycI/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-09-17%2Bat%2B12.08.17%2BPM.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2zcgJktyfVs/Vg0GiBnAh3I/AAAAAAAAB2U/ZlEPucOWJAA/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-09-17%2Bat%2B12.09.18%2BPM.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="216" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2zcgJktyfVs/Vg0GiBnAh3I/AAAAAAAAB2U/ZlEPucOWJAA/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-09-17%2Bat%2B12.09.18%2BPM.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, if you are taking &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; cartilage supplements to prevent cancer, you might want to save your money and in the process, you just might &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;save&lt;/a&gt; a shark.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/8235897978920576358'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/11/do-sharks-get-cancer.html' title='Do sharks get cancer?'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1IMvKt8e1hU/Vg0GgfYnSVI/AAAAAAAAB2E/AqkrhKHNflw/s72-c/P9170039.JPG' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-2513661120554243412</id><published>2015-11-23T11:22:00.002-08:00</published><updated>2015-11-23T11:27:35.604-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='tiger sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='bull sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white sharks'/><title type='text'>Island Of The White Sharks </title><content type='html'>&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-2f3D6eyNZps/Vg0e7mbJQfI/AAAAAAAAB7c/NWjxtS8bJ1A/s1600/_26A7012.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="262" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-2f3D6eyNZps/Vg0e7mbJQfI/AAAAAAAAB7c/NWjxtS8bJ1A/s400/_26A7012.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;helvetica neue&amp;quot; , &amp;quot;arial&amp;quot; , &amp;quot;helvetica&amp;quot; , sans-serif;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: x-small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;helvetica neue&amp;quot; , &amp;quot;arial&amp;quot; , &amp;quot;helvetica&amp;quot; , sans-serif;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: rgb(86.274520% , 34.901960% , 13.333330%); font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Do you want to know what it is like to come to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; and meet the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt;? Read the following trip report and look at the pictures from John Gunn and Katrien De Maertelaere who joined us at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; back in August.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 1"&gt;&lt;div class="section" style="background-color: rgb(100.000000%, 100.000000%, 100.000000%);"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="color: rgb(86.274520% , 34.901960% , 13.333330%); font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 32.000000pt;"&gt;Island Of The White Sharks &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;As we boarded Horizon, the 80 foot long dive boat that would be our home for the next week, we had no idea of the adventures that lay ahead. Fulfilling a life long dream to dive with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt;, I was about to embark on a trip out to Guadalupe Island in Mexico. A rocky desolate island 150 miles west of Baja California, which is now recognized as &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt; font-weight: 600;"&gt;the &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;best place to dive with these wonderful creatures in crystal clear waters. Having recently spent time out at the Farallon Islands (The west coast’s other hub of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White&lt;/a&gt; activity) I couldn’t wait to experience the magic of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;Shark Diver (&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;www.sharkdiver.com&lt;/a&gt;) were our hosts and the crew of the Horizon greeted us warmly as we strolled past the monstrous steel shark cages out on deck and settled into our cosy sleeping quarters. The trip out to Guadalupe isn’t for the light hearted, a 36 hour trek in decent swells (and apparently we had it calm!) but the Horizon was a wonderful vessel and once we’d past through immigration in Ensenada, Mexico we were out in the open ocean, heading due west over some of the richest and biologically diverse stretches of water in the world. Within a couple of hours of leaving the Mexican mainland we were accompanied by a large group of Pilot Whales, who stayed with us for over an hour, breaching out of the water just a few feet from the boat. It was a wonderful start to what we were all hoping would be the adventure of a lifetime.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 2"&gt;&lt;div class="section" style="background-color: rgb(100.000000%, 100.000000%, 100.000000%);"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-PGYlhS2JXfM/VlNdabJ0MUI/AAAAAAAACFQ/w-_t6zHQabA/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.39.03%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="208" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-PGYlhS2JXfM/VlNdabJ0MUI/AAAAAAAACFQ/w-_t6zHQabA/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.39.03%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;After a bumpy couple of nights sleep, we awoke on the second morning to the sounds of clucking steel and rushed up on deck. The cages were slowly being lowered into the water, overshadowed by the towering, volcanic rock face of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. It was quite a sight and it felt only right that one of the world’s largest congregations of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt; had chosen this alien rocky outpost as their hunting ground. After a quick but delicious cooked breakfast (the food on the entire trip was divine!) and an introduction to the cage rotations (we’d be tag teaming one hour in and one hour out of the cage for the next 2 days!) it was time to gear up and get diving! &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-78rIPxe3OCA/VlNdIcs4UvI/AAAAAAAACFI/KLKRXdsnJ0A/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.37.54%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="265" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-78rIPxe3OCA/VlNdIcs4UvI/AAAAAAAACFI/KLKRXdsnJ0A/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.37.54%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;I was part of the first rotation and with the bate lines floating next to the cages and chum being poured over the side of the boat, we anxiously waited for our first glimpse of the world’s oldest apex predator! The hour ticked by without an appearance and the next team of divers jumped in to try their luck. Within minutes we were startled by the soon to be familiar shout, ‘&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;WHITE SHARK&lt;/a&gt;!’ as a huge dark shadow gracefully glided past the boat. I could only imagine the sight from below the surface. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 3"&gt;&lt;div class="section" style="background-color: rgb(100.000000%, 100.000000%, 100.000000%);"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bh62bMu5JnU/VlNb-5-btII/AAAAAAAACE8/Gxc17rjkBYw/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.32.49%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="261" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bh62bMu5JnU/VlNb-5-btII/AAAAAAAACE8/Gxc17rjkBYw/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.32.49%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;There had been no need to panic! Our second dive of the day turned out to be one of the best dives of the entire trip. We were treated to 3 &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;White Sharks&lt;/a&gt;, circling the cages for the full hour. The opportunity to see these animals up close in clear water was truly special. They’re both graceful and terrifying at the same time. A monster from your nightmares, that you can’t take your eyes off. The 14 foot sharks glided inches from the cage, ominously disappearing into the blue, before somehow re-appearing moments later from the completely opposite direction. While at first glance their eyes are black and sinister, a closer look reveals a soft light blue interior that focused in on the divers as the shark glides past. These guys were definitely checking us out! &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 4"&gt;&lt;div class="section" style="background-color: rgb(100.000000%, 100.000000%, 100.000000%);"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DFCW11JxYEQ/VlNbjh4l2iI/AAAAAAAACE0/uY6XxH6YY2c/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.31.13%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="287" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DFCW11JxYEQ/VlNbjh4l2iI/AAAAAAAACE0/uY6XxH6YY2c/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.31.13%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;As rotations merged into each other, the action never stopped and as we experienced more sharks, we were privileged to witness an array of different personalities that each gave a unique interaction. &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; keep a log of all the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;White Sharks&lt;/a&gt; they encounter and name them, as a way of keeping track. Over time, we learned who was who; ‘Legend’ was a mid- sized feisty shark that would charge and breach for the bait, giving the topside divers and crew quite a show. ‘Johnny’ was a more relaxed but larger and proud shark and every now and then we’d be lucky enough to look down into the depths and see the infamous ‘Bruce’, a monstrous male &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;White Shark&lt;/a&gt; circling below.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-2uIXR83jLY8/VlNam9Hu94I/AAAAAAAACEo/gkzVA0DnSkk/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.27.13%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="300" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-2uIXR83jLY8/VlNam9Hu94I/AAAAAAAACEo/gkzVA0DnSkk/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.27.13%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;From the surface, the water was so clear it was like watching the sharks swimming in a pool and from below, the 100+ foot visibility offered photo opportunities I’m yet to encounter anywhere in the world. On our last night we were treated to a fantastic presentation from a couple of local researchers (the only inhabitants on the island, with the exception of a small fishing community) from Pelagios Kakunja Marine Conservation, educating us on the vital science and research currently being done to understand more about the Guadalupe ecosystem and the best ways to protect it in the future. As well as the informative talk, the two researchers showed us a ‘deep sea monster’ that they’d found floating on the surface, a bizarre bottom dwelling creature that we figured out probably belonged to the ‘Frog Fish’ family.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 5"&gt;&lt;div class="section" style="background-color: rgb(100.000000%, 100.000000%, 100.000000%);"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-D9BfYCJdf5c/VlNaY8vpmLI/AAAAAAAACEg/3VwJY7pobwY/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.26.04%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="263" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-D9BfYCJdf5c/VlNaY8vpmLI/AAAAAAAACEg/3VwJY7pobwY/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.26.04%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;Finally, we were treated to up close GoPro footage of a recent &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White&lt;/a&gt; predication on an Elephant Seal at the island (only the third time such an attack had been caught on camera), before we all slunked down to our cabins beneath the waves and looked forward to the final morning of diving before our departure back to the mainland. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;The final morning didn’t disappoint, as we were continuously circled by a large male &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; called ‘Biteface’. At nearly 16 feet in length, he dwarfed the cage as he glided inches from the steel cage and our busy cameras! After lunch the cages were hoisted back onto the Horizon and we set pace at a steady 10 knots, back to San Diego. Within a few hours, just as the sun was setting, we were accompanied by a stunning group of breaching Dolphins, giving the entire group a great opportunity to reflect on this wonderfully rich and wild stretch of ocean and the trip of a lifetime. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-HNNu5SCJeWY/VlNaH-5PUII/AAAAAAAACEY/Gd1V_iijeBA/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.24.33%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-HNNu5SCJeWY/VlNaH-5PUII/AAAAAAAACEY/Gd1V_iijeBA/s400/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-11-23%2Bat%2B10.24.33%2BAM.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 10.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 10.000000pt;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;      &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="page" title="Page 6"&gt;&lt;div class="section" style="background-color: rgb(100.000000%, 100.000000%, 100.000000%);"&gt;&lt;div class="layoutArea"&gt;&lt;div class="column"&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: &amp;quot;baskerville&amp;quot;; font-size: 12.000000pt;"&gt;Will I be returning to Guadalupe? Most certainly, but probably not before my passion for Sharks and underwater photography takes me to the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/tiger-shark-diving/"&gt;Tiger Sharks&lt;/a&gt; of the Bahamas and the resident &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;Bulls Sharks&lt;/a&gt; of Fiji. Take a bow &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;, you well and truly delivered! &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Thank you John and Katrien for coming out with us and writing this great report! It was a pleasure having you on board and we enjoyed introducing you to our "friends" at Guadalupe Island. We are looking forward to taking you to the Bahamas and Fiji for your next shark diving adventure!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white shark&lt;/a&gt; season at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; so far. As &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/08/bigger-than-big-blue-biggest-shark-at.html"&gt;reported earlier&lt;/a&gt;, a lot of our regular visitors have come back again, with "Bite Face" making his 15th straight appearance.&amp;nbsp;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;Along with our old "friends", we have also seen a bunch of new sharks. Three of them have officially been added to the &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/white-shark/"&gt;MCSI photo ID database&lt;/a&gt; during our last science expedition.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Introducing "Luca" a sub adult male, # 171 in our database.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both;
