text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-zA0t1-9bVt0/VgqrdgwPeZI/AAAAAAAAB0k/lKiJJ80GknI/s1600/%2523172%2BFreya%2B1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-zA0t1-9bVt0/VgqrdgwPeZI/AAAAAAAAB0k/lKiJJ80GknI/s400/%2523172%2BFreya%2B1.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"Hunter", a curious and active male is going to be #173&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-mxM352cDpy0/Vgqvf1TInJI/AAAAAAAAB0w/HQtwo4UmdO4/s1600/Hunter.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="220" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-mxM352cDpy0/Vgqvf1TInJI/AAAAAAAAB0w/HQtwo4UmdO4/s400/Hunter.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Along with those 3 above, we have seen at least another 7 sharks that are not in the database yet. I'll let you know, when they get officially added.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want to meet our sharks up close and personal, call us at 619.987.4275 or email staff@sharkdiver.com. The rest of this season is sold out and our 2016 season is already more than 50% booked. Maybe you will be the next person to find a new shark at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-4442164807153144461</id><published>2015-09-18T15:47:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-09-18T20:31:41.962-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='dive'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Guadalupe'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark week'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='marine'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='scuba'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='sightings'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='california'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='mexico'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='phenomenon'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='discovery channel'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='MCSI'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='deep blue'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='ocean'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='sea creatures'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='sharknado'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='diving'/><title type='text'>Talking about Sharks, Feeds the Frenzy</title><content type='html'>&lt;b&gt;A Growing Attraction&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;Some might say diving with sharks is the last thing they would ever want to do...until they do it! For many, it has become an addiction and more and more repeat divers are getting their yearly thrill with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;, based out of &lt;a href="http://www.sandiego.org/"&gt;San Diego&lt;/a&gt;. For 14 years, &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; has been introducing the public (those who are dive certified and not certified) to the underwater world of great white sharks. They don't plan to stop. Why? Because people keep coming to get their 'fix.' The shark phenomenon has continued to rise for the last few years, due to local and national television news and social media coverage, cable television programming, and of course, &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharknado"&gt;silly movies&lt;/a&gt;. The 'News' has put us in touch with shark sightings off the coasts of Australia, South Africa, the Eastern and Western United States, and Guadalupe Island in Mexico; all right at our fingertips.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;The more we talk about sharks, the more popular they become.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Diks_7vSDtA/Vfxh9FPLcgI/AAAAAAAABx8/nI8mbzQykYw/s1600/Shark%2BDiver%2BInterview%2BMG%2B3.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="289" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Diks_7vSDtA/Vfxh9FPLcgI/AAAAAAAABx8/nI8mbzQykYw/s320/Shark%2BDiver%2BInterview%2BMG%2B3.jpg" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Photo: Cindy Michaels&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;Every year, starting the first week of August, &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; takes more than 200 divers to &lt;a href="http://guadalupefund.org/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; to see these misunderstood creatures, up close. During a 5-day adventure, divers fulfill their bucket list items, unique wedding anniversary&amp;nbsp;or honeymoon&amp;nbsp;celebrations, birthday milestones, or childhood dreams. In 2014, Shark Diver's sold out season saw a record number of divers wanting to see great whites, but it was also one of the biggest years for shark encounters at the cages. Things were only going to grow after that. Already, since the company's first dive this year on August 9th, there have been more than 120 great white shark sightings and it is expected that the same amount, if not more, will be seen by the time the 2015 season ends in November.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-edtVM7zQLvA/VfxfHPs5KOI/AAAAAAAABxs/JlF0zivAelc/s1600/Shark%2BDiver%2B2015%2B10.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="213" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-edtVM7zQLvA/VfxfHPs5KOI/AAAAAAAABxs/JlF0zivAelc/s320/Shark%2BDiver%2B2015%2B10.jpg" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;Get to Know Your Sharks&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; has worked with the &lt;a href="http://www.discovery.com/"&gt;Discovery Channel&lt;/a&gt; for some of its &lt;a href="http://www.discovery.com/tv-shows/shark-week/"&gt;Shark Week&lt;/a&gt; episodes as well as countless other operations that partner for filming. But the company's greatest passion is to bring those who have never seen a shark...to the sharks, themselves. For the past 2 seasons, a researcher from the &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/"&gt;Marine Conservation Science Institute&lt;/a&gt; (&lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;MCSI&lt;/a&gt;) in &lt;a href="http://www.sandiego.org/"&gt;San Diego&lt;/a&gt; has joined Shark Diver in educating divers about specific markings, migratory habits, and all the fun stuff you don't learn in school or on television. On the hosted adventures, divers have the opportunity to name any new shark that is spotted, while in the cages. That named shark is then registered in MCSI's &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/sponsor-a-shark/photo-id-book/"&gt;photo database&lt;/a&gt;, which features more than 150 already identified sharks, such as &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/Great-White-Shark-Diving-6891254142/timeline/"&gt;Bite Face, Shredder, and Bruce&lt;/a&gt;. By naming and identifying the new great white, the divers are helping out with MCSI's research; dedicated to conserving and protecting marine resources. Shouldn't naming a shark be on your &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;bucket list&lt;/a&gt;?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-huAuVZHOhJU/VfxjRElviJI/AAAAAAAAByI/Vr_EZe0fXzk/s1600/DSC_1462.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-huAuVZHOhJU/VfxjRElviJI/AAAAAAAAByI/Vr_EZe0fXzk/s320/DSC_1462.JPG" width="212" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Photo: Cindy Michaels&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;What to Expect without Expecting&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;Like other highly feared fish, great whites are unpredictable. There may be curious juveniles that try to bite delicately on the cages, or a large adult that just wants to stroll by slowly to check you out. There is no expecting one behavior or another from these boys and girls. Divers prepare themselves for a scary time, but walk away awe-inspired by what they just witnessed. Every trip reveals something different.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-GjCXGeqnU7A/VfyPvrYt50I/AAAAAAAABy0/4rJSp9W9OFU/s1600/_26A8617.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="213" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-GjCXGeqnU7A/VfyPvrYt50I/AAAAAAAABy0/4rJSp9W9OFU/s320/_26A8617.JPG" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;When you decide that life is too short to only watch sharks on television, venture out on a dive with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;. You will see a great white shark while on your trip or the crew will take you back to Guadalupe Island at no extra charge. It is the company's guarantee. Whether or not Shark Diver sees you year after year, there is a good chance you will never view great white sharks the same way, again.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;~Cindy Michaels&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-family: inherit;"&gt;&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;.&lt;/a&gt;   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark expedition'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark adventure'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Great White Sharks, Dolphins and a "Sea Monster"</title><content type='html'>We just finished another awesome expedition to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. After 14 years of diving there, it never ceases to amaze me, that we keep encountering new things.&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;We had a pleasant trip down to the Island, with mostly calm waters and were accompanied by a pod of pilot whales that stayed with us for a while.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-WT4N_qwg1H0/VeokAlEbOUI/AAAAAAAABwg/vDcCa0rw_AI/s1600/_26A6254.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-WT4N_qwg1H0/VeokAlEbOUI/AAAAAAAABwg/vDcCa0rw_AI/s400/_26A6254.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On our first day of diving, we had "Herman", a good sized adult male &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;white shark&lt;/a&gt;, swim by our cages, just as 2 adult bottle nose dolphins and their baby showed up. As soon as he saw them, he took off like a top fuel race car at the 1/4 mile track. Score one for the dolphins! (unfortunately we don't have any pictures of this)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At the end of our second day, the local researchers came by with a "sea monster" they found floating on the surface. I had no idea that these things existed in our waters. Anyone knows what species this is?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-kp9RdCLesXM/Veoi1DvfxJI/AAAAAAAABwM/Q31CQV3nMVc/s1600/IMG_9803.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="213" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-kp9RdCLesXM/Veoi1DvfxJI/AAAAAAAABwM/Q31CQV3nMVc/s320/IMG_9803.JPG" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Our "Sea Monster"&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We encountered a total of 16 different &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; on our trip and some, like "Legend" and "Herman", really put on a show, swimming by the cages and looking our divers straight into the eyes. Another sea turtle checked out our divers and showed us that they are not afraid to swim with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-rtcB0mQmLPs/VeojtHxfM7I/AAAAAAAABwY/TSiNMaGTm7Q/s1600/GOPR0708.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="220" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-rtcB0mQmLPs/VeojtHxfM7I/AAAAAAAABwY/TSiNMaGTm7Q/s400/GOPR0708.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;The trip home was again flat calm, a fact that was greatly appreciated by our diver. We are leaving again in a few hours for another exciting expedition to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. What will we be seeing this time?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark diving&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-733990121219389885</id><published>2015-08-30T07:58:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-08-30T11:46:23.225-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark scare'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark attack'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='hammerhead shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='aggressive shark'/><title type='text'>"Aggressive" shark closes San Diego Beach</title><content type='html'>We arrived back in San Diego from our last &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Great White Shark&lt;/a&gt; trip just in time for an "aggressive" hammerhead shark to close a popular La Jolla (San Diego) beach.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;According to the &lt;a href="http://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/"&gt;San Diego Union Tribune&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"A hammerhead shark that circled and followed a group of swimmers and  kayakers near La Jolla Shores prompted lifeguards to close a stretch of  water to thousands of beachgoers Saturday afternoon."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://cdn.sandiegouniontrib.com/img/photos/2015/08/29/UTI1872662_r900x493.jpg?122770e84b36f1c039d5c4c2ca15c2d8bc4ecd52" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://cdn.sandiegouniontrib.com/img/photos/2015/08/29/UTI1872662_r900x493.jpg?122770e84b36f1c039d5c4c2ca15c2d8bc4ecd52" height="218" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;A hammerhead shark circles a kayaker near La Jolla Shores Saturday. The  shark's aggressive behavior prompted the beach to close for the  remainder of the day and night.                                                      &lt;i&gt;  — Jimmy Van Evera&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Since these hammerhead sharks are not normally "aggressive" towards humans and usually quite shy, I was surprised to hear that one was actually approaching a group of swimmers.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Upon further reading of the &lt;a href="http://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/news/2015/aug/29/aggressive-shark-closes-la-jolla-beach/"&gt;article&lt;/a&gt;, I found that there was a good reason for the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; to come close to the kayak and the swimmers.&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;“We each caught a yellowfin, and we always bleed them out to keep  them fresher,” said Jimmy Van Evera, who estimated they’d fished for  three hours. “We were paddling back in and we saw this hammerhead pop up  near our kayaks.”&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; It was about 10 yards away, but ventured closer and closer"&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Ok, that explains a lot. Hammerheads, like most sharks love to eat tuna. By bleeding their catch into the water, the fishermen essentially rang the dinner bell for the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; in question. The tuna blood was covering their kayaks and by paddling to shore, the kayak left a scent trail for the shark to follow.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1"&gt;&lt;span data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body"&gt;&lt;span class="UFICommentBody" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.$end:0:$text0:0"&gt; The shark  knows what a tuna looks like and once it sees the kayak, is curious to find out what smells like a  tuna, but looks like a kayak. These hammerheads are not really a threat to humans,  unless they happen to be covered in fish blood.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1"&gt;&lt;span data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body"&gt;&lt;span class="UFICommentBody" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.$end:0:$text0:0"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1"&gt;&lt;span data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body"&gt;&lt;span class="UFICommentBody" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.$end:0:$text4:0"&gt;The headline for this story should have read "Irresponsible fishermen lure &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; close to swimmers", instead of calling the shark aggressive. Read the entire article &lt;a href="http://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/news/2015/aug/29/aggressive-shark-closes-la-jolla-beach/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1"&gt;&lt;span data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body"&gt;&lt;span class="UFICommentBody" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.$end:0:$text4:0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1"&gt;&lt;span data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body"&gt;&lt;span class="UFICommentBody" data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".9z.1:5:1:$comment909868955727089_909884025725582:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.$end:0:$text4:0"&gt;If  a human smells food and goes to check it out, is he/she showing  aggressive behavior? The biggest shark at Guadalupe Island!</title><content type='html'>We just returned from our first expedition to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; this year. I'm happy to report that the big boys are back. Bruce, Jacques, Bite Face and Thor all made it back safely to the island. As big as those sharks are, they were dwarfed by the biggest shark to ever swim by a cage at Guadalupe. On our second day of diving, we encountered the largest fish on earth, a whale shark, swimming alongside a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white shark&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white shark&lt;/a&gt;. You never know, what you are going to see on the ocean. Aside from great whites and the whale shark, we also got a visit from 6 bottle nose dolphins and a couple of green sea turtles.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-92c6GOSy9n0/Vc5F3rVFmSI/AAAAAAAABrA/QsiplHOh4T8/s1600/_26A1148.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-92c6GOSy9n0/Vc5F3rVFmSI/AAAAAAAABrA/QsiplHOh4T8/s400/_26A1148.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It's not only the big boys that are back. We also saw the slightly smaller Hooper, Mau, Horizon, Ace, Micks, Mike, Drogin, Legend, Paul Walker, Seamus, Don Julian, Big and Ian along with the females Sydney and Amiria.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-BFcoaiu_8ys/Vc5CrD66SbI/AAAAAAAABqw/ljkBDRQp-po/s1600/_26A1153.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-BFcoaiu_8ys/Vc5CrD66SbI/AAAAAAAABqw/ljkBDRQp-po/s400/_26A1153.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;Like last year, we also encountered some new sharks. We definitely have another small female and male shark.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I_xDbnTE_RU/Vc4moi83tuI/AAAAAAAABqY/R0YNEgQmlDo/s1600/_26A9456.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I_xDbnTE_RU/Vc4moi83tuI/AAAAAAAABqY/R0YNEgQmlDo/s400/_26A9456.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;We only have a few spaces available for this season. I can't wait to see who is back at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. Is "Shredder" going to be there after being absent for a couple of years?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I-9NAT7UksA/VMpjSjF4ZLI/AAAAAAAABQI/xKxyA4ApMrY/s1600/Shredder%2B1a.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="181" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I-9NAT7UksA/VMpjSjF4ZLI/AAAAAAAABQI/xKxyA4ApMrY/s400/Shredder%2B1a.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Shredder"&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I'm really worried that something happened to him, but since "Quetzalcoatl" (no I did not name him)&lt;br /&gt;once stayed away from Guadalupe Island for 8 years, I still have hope!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%252356.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="300" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s400/%252356.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Quetzalcoatl"&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What about our regulars like "Bruce", "Jacques", "Bite-Face", "Johnny" etc.? Who is making an appearance this season?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-2K-ZhIgoC0c/UwjAgMeT9II/AAAAAAAAAt8/g_K46Hkjz80/s1600/DSC_0100c.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="310" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-2K-ZhIgoC0c/UwjAgMeT9II/AAAAAAAAAt8/g_K46Hkjz80/s400/DSC_0100c.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Jacques" one of our regulars.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Who is going to get hurt this season?&amp;nbsp; It never ceases to amaze me, how rough they play with each other.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-9WwfkWgjaW8/VUT2u0ZpXFI/AAAAAAAABZM/c1ISM723Etc/s1600/Bruce%2Bwith%2Bbite.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="285" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-9WwfkWgjaW8/VUT2u0ZpXFI/AAAAAAAABZM/c1ISM723Etc/s400/Bruce%2Bwith%2Bbite.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Bruce" a couple of years ago&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But don't worry, they have an amazing ability to heal. Just look at the picture of "Bruce" below!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-npLTElMIUwY/VXHyA16CaVI/AAAAAAAABds/UVTI415Qet4/s1600/1-96%2B3.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="240" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-npLTElMIUwY/VXHyA16CaVI/AAAAAAAABds/UVTI415Qet4/s400/1-96%2B3.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Bruce" with barely a scar from his bite.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We never know who is going to be back. Every year we encounter new sharks and see old "friends". Right now, we have more than 170 individual great white sharks in our database, with a handful having been there every season, since 2001.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are interested in learning more about the photo id database of our &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt;, check out &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/white-shark/"&gt;MCSI's website here&lt;/a&gt;. We also have only 2 spaces open on our Sept. 14-19 science expedition with &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Nicole Nasby-Lucas&lt;/a&gt;, the scientist responsible for the database.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To join us on the science expedition, call us at 619.887.4275 or email &lt;a href="mailto:staff@sharkdiver.com"&gt;staff@sharkdiver.com&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We also have limited openings on our Aug 30, Sept. 4 and Sept. 9 expedition.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. you're going to love this movie!</title><content type='html'>I had the chance to watch David Diley's movie "&lt;a href="http://www.ofsharkandman.com/"&gt;Of Shark &amp;amp; Man&lt;/a&gt;" and absolutely loved it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is how the filmmaker describes the movie.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;David Diley is a thirty-two year old man, trapped in a dead end job  in England's industrial north and his life is going nowhere. He does  however, have a lifelong dream...&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;Should David follow the advice of everyone around him and forget  about it, or should he risk everything and against all the odds, take  his one chance to fulfill his greatest ambition, an ambition which finds  him in the middle of a feeding frenzy with sixty of the world's most  dangerous sharks?&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-QEiXAP98Ic0/U35OP3ga7TI/AAAAAAAAA48/-CpUN98Y2-s/s1600/XD5V0095.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="242" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-QEiXAP98Ic0/U35OP3ga7TI/AAAAAAAAA48/-CpUN98Y2-s/s400/XD5V0095.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;“Of Shark and Man” is a ground breaking film about one man's journey  to get closer than anyone thought possible, to the world's biggest Bull  Sharks and tell the incredible untold story of Shark Reef in Fiji, one  of the greatest marine conservation successes of all time.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;“Of Shark and Man” is an epic, incredibly ambitious and cinematic  love letter to the world's most feared predator, in which, for once, the  shark is the hero.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To me it is much more than just a movie about &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; and man, it is about following your dreams, overcoming obstacles and never giving up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is the trailer. term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='sharknado'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Are the sharks going to be safe at Guadalupe Island?</title><content type='html'>&lt;a href="http://www.syfy.com/sharknado3"&gt;Sharknado 3&lt;/a&gt; airs tonight on the &lt;a href="http://www.syfy.com/"&gt;SCIFY&lt;/a&gt; channel. At the rate those Sharknado's remove the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks &lt;/a&gt;from the water, this might well be the last chance to see them live at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-STKN1uisq_8/Va_Sq6-D29I/AAAAAAAABm8/uMKA7psWfFE/s1600/GWS%2Bfrontal%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="263" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-STKN1uisq_8/Va_Sq6-D29I/AAAAAAAABm8/uMKA7psWfFE/s400/GWS%2Bfrontal%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When &lt;a href="http://www.briankilmeade.com/"&gt;Brian Kilmeade&lt;/a&gt;, from &lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/on-air/fox-and-friends/"&gt;FOX and friends&lt;/a&gt; was surprised that the water at a South African surf contest wasn't clear of sharks, he must have had thought that after Sharknado 2, all the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; were gone already. Luckily, that was not the case. We saw them in record numbers at Guadalupe Island last season.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-iu9rl1x2JAk/Va_SyzqlG6I/AAAAAAAABnE/yI3owBL8mSc/s1600/close%2Bup%2Bwith%2Bcamera%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="273" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-iu9rl1x2JAk/Va_SyzqlG6I/AAAAAAAABnE/yI3owBL8mSc/s400/close%2Bup%2Bwith%2Bcamera%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Just to make sure you visit the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;, before they all get sucked out of the water. Call us at 619.887.4275 or email staff@sharkdiver.com for more information, or to reserve your spot.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-wk9kGqtjyec/Va_S9GkPyEI/AAAAAAAABnM/57sJt8boApM/s1600/Dr.%2BBob%252C%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-wk9kGqtjyec/Va_S9GkPyEI/AAAAAAAABnM/57sJt8boApM/s400/Dr.%2BBob%252C%2Bblog%2Bres.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Stay safe tonight and let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-2660115639425890854</id><published>2015-07-17T10:38:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-07-17T10:38:14.646-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='biggest shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark week'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='mega shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Biggest White Shark ever filmed?</title><content type='html'>The &lt;a href="http://www.discovery.com/"&gt;Discovery Channel&lt;/a&gt; promised us a better quality of programming for &lt;a href="http://www.discovery.com/tv-shows/shark-week/tv-shows/tv-shows/"&gt;"Shark Week"&lt;/a&gt; this season, so I was curious to see what they would offer. One of their episodes was titled "Island of the Mega Shark". So who, or what, is that mega shark?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-egWM-d5LK1E/Vak9DUgSguI/AAAAAAAABmA/1uTgKHjxS_k/s1600/1-5%2B2.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="235" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-egWM-d5LK1E/Vak9DUgSguI/AAAAAAAABmA/1uTgKHjxS_k/s320/1-5%2B2.JPG" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When that "Mega Shark" swims under the cage Dickie Chivell exclaims that &lt;i&gt;"this is the biggest shark I've ever seen in my life"&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;"you have to make up a new word for how big this shark is." &lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well Dickie, we have a word for that "Mega Shark". We call her "Lucy". She is easily identified by her mangled tail and is certainly a big shark, but more in the 17 ft range and definitely not over 20 ft. If this is the biggest shark you have ever seen in your life, you should really spend some more time at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; and see the really big sharks.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aXYhZ1u0Bq0/VakkFkDZ3NI/AAAAAAAABlQ/IoZ-D-l9GW4/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.48.22%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="206" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aXYhZ1u0Bq0/VakkFkDZ3NI/AAAAAAAABlQ/IoZ-D-l9GW4/s320/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.48.22%2BAM.png" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Lucy" is easily identified by her tail.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Imagine my surprise (sharkasm intended) when, a little later in the clip,  I found out that this "Mega Shark" is actually more than one shark. The second shark is "Tail Scratch", again a large shark, but hardly 20 ft. When she was measured in 2009, she was 15 ft, which would make her between 16 and 17 ft. now. She is not even close to being the biggest shark that we regularly see at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. The &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/"&gt;Marine Conservation Science Institute&lt;/a&gt; has a photo &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/white-shark/"&gt;ID database&lt;/a&gt; that catalogs every shark that we have seen at Guadalupe Island in the past 15 years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-3-2UK19RGWQ/Vakkx4FLlNI/AAAAAAAABlY/wY4iZ01HGh4/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.49.04%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="235" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-3-2UK19RGWQ/Vakkx4FLlNI/AAAAAAAABlY/wY4iZ01HGh4/s320/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.49.04%2BAM.png" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When you look at the pelvic fin area, you can clearly identify her. As you can see from the pictures below, it is the same shark.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RZtyoILeT9E/VakmhsINpdI/AAAAAAAABls/u_G9EaCK48s/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.59.36%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RZtyoILeT9E/VakmhsINpdI/AAAAAAAABls/u_G9EaCK48s/s320/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.59.36%2BAM.png" width="292" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Screen shot from video&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rXxjVofwPhQ/VaklTZtNrRI/AAAAAAAABlg/a3H0hA1QBkM/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.53.48%2BAM.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="261" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rXxjVofwPhQ/VaklTZtNrRI/AAAAAAAABlg/a3H0hA1QBkM/s320/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-07-17%2Bat%2B8.53.48%2BAM.png" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Tail Scratch (from Shark ID book) &lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;Watch the video below from youtube. It shows the typical Jeff Kurr, and ABC4 stuff. If you want us to actually believe that there is a mega shark at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;, at least improve your editing a little so it is not painfully obvious that you are showing more than one shark.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;object width="320" height="266" what kind of "experts" you are when it comes to great white sharks.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span id="goog_1964946539"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span id="goog_1964946539"&gt;For photo ID book &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/sponsor-a-shark/photo-id-book/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;. It is a great resource for anyone watching "Shark Week" or who's going to Guadalupe Island. Shark Diver is proud to support Nicole's research and has her hosting our &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-science-expedition"&gt;special science expeditions&lt;/a&gt; to Guadalupe Island each year.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span id="goog_1964946539"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span id="goog_1964946539"&gt;Let's go shark diving and experience these magnificent animals up close and personal. Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Valerie Taylor'/><title type='text'>Valerie Taylor, the most glamorous shark advocate in the world</title><content type='html'>With the 40th anniversary of the release of "Jaws", "&lt;a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/"&gt;The Telegraph&lt;/a&gt;" has a very nice article on &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Ron-And-Valerie-Taylor/133552650042610"&gt;Valerie Taylor&lt;/a&gt;. She, together with her late husband Ron, was an underwater videographer for Steven Spielberg's "Jaws".&amp;nbsp; The article's headline calls her &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;"The most glamorous shark hunter in the world".&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt; Though I think "The most glamorous shark advocate in the world" is a much more fitting title, the article itself &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;does a great job of telling Valerie's life story. From her  beginning as a champion spearfisher to one of the world's leading  advocates for conservation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent-lax1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xfa1/v/t1.0-9/391975_417111221686750_1321330098_n.jpg?oh=945bd503259d4a3f65c55c1ebe453597&amp;amp;oe=55EB64B0" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="214" src="https://scontent-lax1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xfa1/v/t1.0-9/391975_417111221686750_1321330098_n.jpg?oh=945bd503259d4a3f65c55c1ebe453597&amp;amp;oe=55EB64B0" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The article shows to how Valerie and Ron were being chastised for demonizing sharks &lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;"Within the marine conservation world, Ron and Valerie were vilified for  their role in a movie that demonised sharks. “It caused the most  incredible slaughter of innocent sharks that would never have hurt  anybody, and they tried to blame Ron and me,” says Valerie. “To us, Jaws  was a fictitious story about a fictitious shark. You don’t go to New  York and expect to see King Kong hanging from the Empire State Building.  But Jaws was so well done that people took it to heart.” &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It talks about why they decided to become conservationists &lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;"It was at the&lt;a href="http://auf.com.au/sports/spearfishing/" target="_blank"&gt; Australian Spearfishing Championship in Queensland in 1969&lt;/a&gt; that the pair had an epiphany. “We looked at all these beautiful  tropical fish lying on the beach waiting to be weighed in, and I  thought, 'What have we done?’ Ron said to me, 'This is terrible. We’re  making a living filming beautiful marine animals and then for sport  we’re killing them.’” They won the competition but never fished again,  instead using their celebrity status to raise awareness. “I was young  and beautiful and had long blonde hair, and I’d jump into the sea with  any animal and do anything, so I was very successful in the field of  conservation,” Valerie says, wryly."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;It shows that eventually they became known as conservationist. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;"By the 1980s, Ron and Valerie - along with fellow conservationists  Benchley and his wife Wendy - had regained the high regard of the  international conservation community. They successfully lobbied the  Australian government to protect the Coral Sea Islands off Queensland,  and their documentary films about the wreck of the Yongala, an iconic  diving site, and the &lt;a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/travel/destinations/australiaandpacific/australia/10148532/The-Great-Barrier-Reef-Australia-Trip-of-a-Lifetime.html" target="_blank"&gt;Great Barrier Reef&lt;/a&gt;,  proved instrumental in promoting the conservation of reefs. Valerie,  who still lives in Sydney, has continued her conservation efforts alone  since Ron’s death, as well as continuing to dive with sharks".&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Valerie is still a very  active diver, despite the fact that she'll be 80 this November. My  favorite part is how the &lt;a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/film/11700946/The-most-glamorous-shark-hunter-in-the-world.htm"&gt;article&lt;/a&gt; starts. &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"W&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;hen I tentatively ask 79-year-old Valerie Taylor if she still  scuba-dives, she erupts with incredulous horror. “Oh my God, yes! What  else would I do?"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Just a few weeks ago Valerie was diving with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;bull sharks&lt;/a&gt; in Fiji. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The picture below shows her diving with the late &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/06/sad-news-out-of-fiji.html"&gt;Rus&lt;/a&gt;i&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt; at the "&lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/conservation/shark-reef-marine-reserve"&gt;Shark Reef Marine Reserve&lt;/a&gt;",&amp;nbsp; a dive that she describes as "&lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;The best shark dive in the world!&lt;/a&gt;"&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-nmg1N_0ZiYY/VYaBMguZLDI/AAAAAAAAOTo/qmhSrt7ube4/s1600/three%2Bwise%2Bones.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="205" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-nmg1N_0ZiYY/VYaBMguZLDI/AAAAAAAAOTo/qmhSrt7ube4/s1600/three%2Bwise%2Bones.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;picture by &lt;a href="http://www.predapix.com/"&gt;Sam Cahir "predapix"&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;You can read Valerie's life story &lt;a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/film/11700946/The-most-glamorous-shark-hunter-in-the-world.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt; it gives you a great view of who Valerie Taylor is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want to dive with sharks yourself, give us a call at 619.887.4275 or email us at staff@sharkdiver.com and we'll be happy to give you all the info you need to make your dream a reality.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;www.sharkdiver.com&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Shark Week at Guadalupe</title><content type='html'>With "&lt;a href="http://www.discovery.com/tv-shows/shark-week/"&gt;Shark Week&lt;/a&gt;" coming up, a lot of you are probably dreaming about what it would be like to be part of the show. How would it feel to come face to face with a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-film-expedition/"&gt;great white shark&lt;/a&gt;? How awesome would it be to show your friends a movie of you experiencing a "&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving"&gt;real shark week&lt;/a&gt;"?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RfBSXXQOjAQ/VYrn_YIwk3I/AAAAAAAABg0/WaacOnuydWs/s1600/1-36.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RfBSXXQOjAQ/VYrn_YIwk3I/AAAAAAAABg0/WaacOnuydWs/s400/1-36.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;Well, you can make that dream a reality. We have 2 special &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-film-expedition/"&gt;film expeditions&lt;/a&gt; to Guadalupe coming up on September 4-9 and 9-14-2014. &lt;b&gt;Peter Kragh,&lt;/b&gt; &lt;b&gt;Emmy Award winner 2013 for Outstanding Cinematography on Nat Geo's "Untamed Americas"&lt;/b&gt;, who was also part of many "shark week" specials, is leading those expeditions. He will film you with those great white sharks and show you the tricks of the trade. Just imagine how awesome it will be to experience these amazing creatures in the water, and have a movie to show to your friends. It will be an experience of a lifetime with memories you'll never forget. The next time you'll talk about "shark week", you'll be telling your friends about the time this shark swam by and looked you straight into the eyes.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table (Rusiate-Balenagasau) from &lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;Beqa Adventure Divers&lt;/a&gt; has passed away.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; &lt;/b&gt;I just got back from Fiji a few weeks ago and had the privilege to dive with Rusi and his beloved bull sharks. I can't say I knew him well, but his love for the sharks and his dedication to their conservation was obvious. I fondly remember watching him feed his sharks and it will not be the same without him.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FBzTfEbvh94/VYcxZSrnN-I/AAAAAAAABgE/5n-PCnfEY1U/s1600/_26A3001.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FBzTfEbvh94/VYcxZSrnN-I/AAAAAAAABgE/5n-PCnfEY1U/s400/_26A3001.JPG" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Rusi 1960-2015&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My sincere condolences go out to his family, friends and all the guys and gals at &lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;Beqa Adventure Divers.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Rest in peace Rusi!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-2290879510244440529</id><published>2015-06-18T10:01:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-06-18T10:02:14.857-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='project aware'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='plastic waste'/><title type='text'>Anyone can help save sharks</title><content type='html'>Do you want to help save &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, but think there is nothing you can do, because you live too far from the Ocean? Do you think "I'm alone, what possible difference can I make"?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, there is good news! You can do something!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.padi.com/"&gt;PADI&lt;/a&gt;, the professional association of dive instructors, through their Project Aware has launched a campaign to raise awareness for the huge problem plastic garbage entering the oceans presents.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%252356.jpg" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="300" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s400/%252356.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;Please help to save me! Thank you!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;From &lt;span style="color: #38761d;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.projectaware.org/"&gt;Project Aware&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Did you know that a staggering 250 million metric tons of plastic could  make its way to the ocean in the next 10 years? And that as much as 70  percent of marine litter has been estimated to end up on the seabed.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;Marine  debris comes from many land and ocean sources. Yet few of us understand  that our trash can travel over land, down streams, rivers and storm  drains to the ocean.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;That's why Project AWARE is  collecting marine debris data from divers. We're painting a clear  picture of the underwater trash that threatens ocean life and building a  case against ocean trash for all to see.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Follow &lt;b&gt;The Ugly Journey of Our Trash&lt;/b&gt; to discover more about its journey to the ocean and its dangerous impact on our marine life. &lt;a href="http://www.projectaware.org/resource/ugly-journey-our-trash" target="_blank"&gt;Poster versions available &lt;/a&gt;in Chinese, Korean, Dutch, German, Italian, French, Spanish and Russian.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4 style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Watch and Share the Ugly Journey of Our Trash.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;h4 style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" class="YOUTUBE-iframe-video" data-thumbnail-src="https://i.ytimg.com/vi/fzFqELV3P3w/0.jpg" frameborder="0" height="433" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/fzFqELV3P3w?feature=player_embedded" width="520"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;h4 style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;h4 style="line-height: 18.003999710083px;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Help by educating your community, friends and colleagues on how our rubbish becomes the ocean's problem. &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.projectaware.org/sites/default/files/imce/UglyJourneyofTrash_Infographic_webfinal.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.projectaware.org/sites/default/files/imce/UglyJourneyofTrash_Infographic_webfinal.png" height="1920" width="477" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf &lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt; is running &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;great white shark expeditions &lt;/a&gt;to Guadalupe Island from August - November, &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/tiger-shark-diving/"&gt;tiger shark&lt;/a&gt; dives in the Bahamas from April - November and &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;bull shark&lt;/a&gt; trips to Fiji from May - June.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='good shark policy'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='california lifeguard'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='stupid headlines'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white shark'/><title type='text'>White Sharks Shock California Lifeguards?</title><content type='html'>&lt;div class="entry-title single-title" itemprop="headline"&gt;The &lt;a href="http://www.inquisitr.com/"&gt;Inquisitr&lt;/a&gt;&lt;i&gt;'&lt;/i&gt;s headline reads &lt;b&gt;"&lt;i&gt;Shark Drone Shock Lifeguards"&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="entry-title single-title" itemprop="headline"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/div&gt;They report:&amp;nbsp; &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"A new shark drone used by Southland lifeguards in California reveal  shocking evidence of the number of sharks swimming near the shoreline at  Seal Beach. It wasn’t something lifeguards there were prepared to see."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-C12LjeeIq5E/VYG1a6LpTbI/AAAAAAAABfQ/nxjNdUyNj78/s1600/1-218.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="213" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-C12LjeeIq5E/VYG1a6LpTbI/AAAAAAAABfQ/nxjNdUyNj78/s320/1-218.JPG" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Imagine the shock these lifeguards must have felt. Who knew that there were &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; in the water? Where have these guys been lifeguarding all their lives? At a pool?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Actually, when reading the &lt;a href="http://www.inquisitr.com/2179578/shark-drone-shock-lifeguards-multiple-5-to-6-foot-great-white-sharks-pack-near-california-shoreline/"&gt;article&lt;/a&gt;, you'll find out that the lifeguards are perfectly capable and were not "shocked" by the drone footage. They write: &lt;/span&gt;"The Chief Seal Beach Lifeguard, Joe Bailey, tells &lt;em&gt;CBS News Los Angeles&lt;/em&gt;&amp;nbsp; This morning, we launched it and 10 minutes later, we knew there were 10 to 12 sharks all in the Surfside [Beach] area" &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The article further states: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;"Bailey loves the shark drone. It’s easy and safe for everyone to see where the creatures are and when to steer clear of them.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;“It works great. It flies up about 100 feet, looks down a  wide area, and when we see the shadows, we’ll go down and focus in on  them.”&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;A juvenile Great White in waist-high water at Surfside was captured  by the drone Monday morning. At the time, there weren’t any swimmers in  the water."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;And here is my favorite part of Joe Bailey's statement according to the Inquisitor &lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;“If we get bigger sharks or we get sharks that are aggressive, we’re  actually going to close the water. But right now, we have sharks that  are 5- to 6-feet long, non-aggressive, acting like normal sharks,  feeding on bottom fish, doing exactly what we would expect them to do.  That’s why we have it posted just to let people know that they are  there.”&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Great response Joe Bailey! No hype, no scaring anyone and promising a reasonable response, should there be any potentially dangerous sharks coming too close to swimmers. I believe that closing a beach for a period of time is the best response to the sighting of a potentially dangerous shark.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ey889uHYIAg/VYG1nsfn6MI/AAAAAAAABfY/g74G6Jbu2v4/s1600/1-5.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="176" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ey889uHYIAg/VYG1nsfn6MI/AAAAAAAABfY/g74G6Jbu2v4/s320/1-5.JPG" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Overall a good article, if only they could find a headline that is not in direct conflict with the article. Maybe something like "Lifeguards NOT worried about white sharks swimming off the coast"?&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Read the entire article&lt;a href="http://www.inquisitr.com/2179578/shark-drone-shock-lifeguards-multiple-5-to-6-foot-great-white-sharks-pack-near-california-shoreline/"&gt; here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver &lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; is running &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;great white shark expeditions &lt;/a&gt;to Guadalupe Island from August - November, &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/tiger-shark-diving/"&gt;tiger shark&lt;/a&gt; dives in the Bahamas from April - November and &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;bull shark&lt;/a&gt; trips to Fiji from May - June.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-C12LjeeIq5E/VYG1a6LpTbI/AAAAAAAABfQ/nxjNdUyNj78/s72-c/1-218.JPG' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-8249299814764619520</id><published>2015-06-15T11:09:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-06-15T11:09:13.395-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark attack'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='tiger shark'/><title type='text'>Shark attack in North Carolina</title><content type='html'>Yesterday, two teenagers were bit by a shark in North Carolina and got severely hurt. This serves as a reminder that, no matter how much we may love these &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, they are not harmless pets. We have to stop portraying them as either mindless killers or harmless pets that just want to be hugged.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://i1.wp.com/newsorigin.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/shark-attack-north-carolina-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://i1.wp.com/newsorigin.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/shark-attack-north-carolina-1.jpg" height="228" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://i1.wp.com/newsorigin.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/shark-attack-north-carolina-1.jpg"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;Before I say anything else, I want to send my best wishes to the victims of these attacks. Regardless of how rare shark attacks are, it doesn't help them that the chances of  getting bit are slim. They got hurt and have to live with the  consequences for the rest of their lives.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If we want to protect these awesome and important predators, we have to  start portraying them the way they are. We have to educate people and  give them a real understanding of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;. If we keep telling them that  these sharks are harmless and just want to be hugged, we loose  credibility, every time someone gets bit. We have to acknowledge that  sharks are not harmless. We have to say that there is no need for  fear, but that we have to respect them. Every time we post pictures of  bikini clad "shark whisperers" holding on to a great white shark and try telling people how harmless they are, we  just reinforce their belief that we are out of touch with reality. When we do that, people will not listen to us, when we tell them how important the shark  are to a healthy ocean environment.&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-R4D0UixMG-s/UkxA1EpYYRI/AAAAAAAAAT8/zlNwh3SWdGo/s1600/DSC_0057.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="312" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-R4D0UixMG-s/UkxA1EpYYRI/AAAAAAAAAT8/zlNwh3SWdGo/s320/DSC_0057.jpg" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We have to acknowledge that sharks do occasionally attack, but let's put things into perspective.&amp;nbsp; Time after time, people point out things that are more dangerous and kill more people than sharks each year. I'm actually hard pressed to find something that kills fewer people than sharks do.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So why is it that people are generally afraid of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;? When we go into the water, we are in an environment that is foreign to us and people tend to be afraid of what they don't know. Our fear of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; is similar to our fear of flying. Even though  airplanes are the safest form of transportation, there are more people  afraid of flying than taking any other mode of transportation.&amp;nbsp; Part of the reason is that just like  when a plane crashes, every time there is a shark attack, the news goes  around the world and creates a perception that sharks are more  dangerous than they really are.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Every time we go into the Ocean, we have a chance to see a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; and an  even greater chance to be seen by one, yet shark attacks remain  extremely rare. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; has been diving with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; for 15 years. We never forget that we are dealing with predators and conduct all our dives with safety in mind. When diving with white sharks, we use cages. When we dive with tiger and bull sharks, we have strict protocols in place to make sure all our divers have a safe and exciting experience. By showing our divers that we use a safety protocol, we are also telling them that we have to respect those sharks and that they are not harmless pets.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-dzRJXP49SnM/U_j4zA48zmI/AAAAAAAABDk/FC-C2nQZkw4/s1600/tiffany-4.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="240" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-dzRJXP49SnM/U_j4zA48zmI/AAAAAAAABDk/FC-C2nQZkw4/s320/tiffany-4.JPG" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Meeting the sharks from the safety of a cage!&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When we tell people about &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, let's tell them the truth. Tell them  that we have to be aware and take reasonable precautions when going into  the ocean. Tell them that we shouldn't touch them, pull them by their  tail or ride them and most importantly, let's lead by example. Stop  promoting these irresponsible divers who touch, ride and hug the sharks,  by not sharing their self aggrandizing pictures and videos.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-V4T3pkuqM4k/U_kNDFmFtwI/AAAAAAAABEE/qTLNEBRSXsY/s1600/1-68.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="195" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-V4T3pkuqM4k/U_kNDFmFtwI/AAAAAAAABEE/qTLNEBRSXsY/s320/1-68.JPG" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Great White Shark with some "love" bites.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;I've been diving with sharks for a long time and absolutely love them. But as I always tell our divers, "Make no mistake, I love these sharks, but it's NOT a mutual feeling". If you love sharks, love them for what they are, don't humanize them, don't make them into something they are not. If you try to make them out to be something they are not, you don't really love them. You want them to be something they are not.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go and meet those sharks!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver &lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds.
